      <div style="right:0" class="readable stacked" id="description">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer7454097380133411409">The story of a travel-hating writer of travel books, Macon Leafy, who systematically avoids adventure... until he meets the frizzy-haired, stiletto-heeled, astonishing Muriel (she's trying to train his unmanageable Welsh corgi, Edward), who up-ends Macon's world and thrusts him into engagement with life. Anne Tyler's most famous best seller.<br />Winner of the 1985 National Book</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7454097380133411409">The story of a travel-hating writer of travel books, Macon Leafy, who systematically avoids adventure... until he meets the frizzy-haired, stiletto-heeled, astonishing Muriel (she's trying to train his unmanageable Welsh corgi, Edward), who up-ends Macon's world and thrusts him into engagement with life. Anne Tyler's most famous best seller.<br />Winner of the 1985 National Book Critics Circle Award for Fiction. 2 cassettes.</span>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });
      $('span_class_actionlink_sort_span_default_tip_968').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {

          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });

      <a href="/user/show/240603-ellen" class="user" title="Ellen">Ellen</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer7299527">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6186683428823213955">It looks like I'm in the minority here, but I really did not enjoy this book. I couldn't sympathize with any of the characters. I thought Macon was whiny and indecisive. I couldn't be compelled to care about what he wanted, mostly because it was never made clear to me exactly what that was. He just seemed to bump along with whatever happened. <br /><br />More than anything else, my problem with this book is that nothing happened. I kept thinking that possibly in the next chapter Macon would act in some way</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6186683428823213955">It looks like I'm in the minority here, but I really did not enjoy this book. I couldn't sympathize with any of the characters. I thought Macon was whiny and indecisive. I couldn't be compelled to care about what he wanted, mostly because it was never made clear to me exactly what that was. He just seemed to bump along with whatever happened. <br /><br />More than anything else, my problem with this book is that nothing happened. I kept thinking that possibly in the next chapter Macon would act in some way to change his own destiny, but nope. Nothing even happened in the end, the book just seemed to stop. </span>

And much of the book is about how our identities are shaped by the people we are with and the story we tell ourselves about who we are when we are with them. This isn't a book you read for plot.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_64050373">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/64050373" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2156200-k-d-absolutely" class="left imgcol" title="K.D. Absolutely"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1449978413p2/2156200.jpg" alt="K.D. Absolutely" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/64050373?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 16, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2156200-k-d-absolutely" class="user" title="K.D. Absolutely">K.D. Absolutely</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/60792.The_Accidental_Tourist" title="Paperback 9780345452009" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to K.D. by: </span>
      501 Must Read Books (Modern Fiction)
  </div>



          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2156200-k-d-absolutely?shelf=1001-core" class="actionLinkLite">1001-core</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2156200-k-d-absolutely?shelf=501" class="actionLinkLite">501</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2156200-k-d-absolutely?shelf=pulitzer" class="actionLinkLite">pulitzer</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2156200-k-d-absolutely?shelf=tragicomic" class="actionLinkLite">tragicomic</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2156200-k-d-absolutely?shelf=family-drama" class="actionLinkLite">family-drama</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a onclick="Effect.toggle('reviewTextContainer64050373'); return false;" href="#">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span style="display:none" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer64050373">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12470362690364167892">“Burying one’s child is against the flow of nature,” said the wife of the Speaker of the House (Philippine Congress) in her eulogy for her 16-year old daughter several years ago. Her only daughter got burned when their short-circuited Christmas tree went in flames. The clueless poor daughter was sleeping and got trapped inside her room. No one was with here in the house when that happened.<br /><br />This is one thought that, whenever it crosses my mind, I always whisk away immediately: <em>the death of my chil</em></span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12470362690364167892">“Burying one’s child is against the flow of nature,” said the wife of the Speaker of the House (Philippine Congress) in her eulogy for her 16-year old daughter several years ago. Her only daughter got burned when their short-circuited Christmas tree went in flames. The clueless poor daughter was sleeping and got trapped inside her room. No one was with here in the house when that happened.<br /><br />This is one thought that, whenever it crosses my mind, I always whisk away immediately: <em>the death of my child.</em> Typing it here even feels wrong as I remember reading that mind has that power to attract what you always think of. I just don't know what to do if this happens. I might as well kill myself, I guess. However, this thing happens. It’s one of the sad realities of life. Once we are born, we can die <em>anytime</em>. In fact, I have some friends and acquaintances whose children died ahead of them. <br /><br />I also read and liked books that have this as its main or underlying theme. <em>Ordinary People</em> (1976) by Judith Guest was my first. The older son (Buck) died while sailing with the younger son (Conrad) and the unspoken guilt of the son and the unexpressed emotion of the parents blaming the younger son who survived was so powerful that when it was made into a movie, it won the Academy Awards for Best Picture. That was in 1980.<br /><br />Second, was a book that I read a couple of years back and topped my list of my favorites for that year: <em>What I Loved</em> (2003) by Siri Husvedt. The grief is also not as openly expressed as in Ordinary People but the child who died was their only one and there was no one to blame as the death was an accident. Similarly, the devastated couple separated and the father tried to see his dead child from same-age children of his friends or even strangers. In this book, <em>The Accidental Tourist</em>, the father, <strong>Macon Leary</strong> starts to withdraw to his own world <em>he would imagine that his whole body was enclosed in a cast and people would peep into the hole in his eyes and would asked “Macon, are you there?”</em> However, Tyler's story went further: Macon seems to belief that the soul of his dead son, <strong>Ethan</strong> remains in his son’s dog, <strong>Edward</strong> and no matter how strange or brutal the dog behaves, he keeps it and even hires a dog-trainer <strong>Muriel</strong> to tame the dog.<br /><br /><em>The Accidental Tourist</em> was the 1985 novel by Anne Tyler (born 1941). A finalist at Pulitzer Prize and won the National Book Critics Award Circle for Fiction. the novel was adapted into a 1988 award-winning film starring William Hurt (as Macon Leary), Kathleen Turner (Sarah, his estranged wife) and Geena Davis (Muriel, the dog trainer). Davis won the Best Actress in a Supporting Role in this film for the succeeding year’s Academy Awards. <br /><br />This is my first Anne Tyler novel. Her writing is straightforward. No-frills yet incandescently clear. It’s an easy read. You’ll have a feeling that you are watching a movie (although I missed this film but I will not forego a chance of seeing it). Her strength seemingly is her strong way of building her characters. She goes inside their minds and she seems to have the ability to know how the character should behave in the circumstances that they are in. Her women characters are not stereotyped: they can be as brutal as <strong>Sandra</strong> leaving Macon to his solitude, as funny yet decisive as <strong>Muriel</strong> who fights for her love and her son Alexander or as eccentric but loyal, vulnerable yet loving as <strong>Rose</strong> who arranges her groceries in alphabetical order and cries over the fact that her brothers would not want to eat her cooked-overnight-in-low-fire turkey. Then there are the Leary brothers: Macon (the father), Charles and Porter and they all are poor in direction that they always get lost even if they are just going to the corner store. This book is peppered with many memorable characters that I had a feeling that I was standing in front of a buffet table and I am confused which one to put on my plate as my favorite.<br /><br />I used to ignore the books of Anne Tyler but next time that I see <em>Dinner at the Homesick Restaurant</em> that Tyler said to be her best work or <em>Breathing Lessons</em> that won the Pulitzer Prize in 1989, I will surely buy them right there and then. Be it bargain or regular-priced. Anne Tyler can surely give back the value of every penny you have in your pocket.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12470362690364167892">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_167999469">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/167999469" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4542979-kim" class="left imgcol" title="Kim"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1451622200p2/4542979.jpg" alt="Kim" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/167999469?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 03, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4542979-kim" class="user" title="Kim">Kim</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/910576.The_Accidental_Tourist" title="Paperback 9780140083408" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/4542979-kim?shelf=buddy-reads-with-jemidar" class="actionLinkLite">buddy-reads-with-jemidar</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4542979-kim?shelf=re-read" class="actionLinkLite">re-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer167999469">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer962855496904943897">This is a warm, wise, funny, heart-breaking and ultimately life-affirming book. In Macon Leary, the man who writes travel books for people who hate to travel, Tyler has created an amazing character. His damaged psyche, his vulnerability, the gradual changes in his character and outlook as he starts to connect with the messiness of living leap off the page. This book makes me laugh out loud one moment and brings tears to my eyes the next. Although Macon is the centre of the novel, the supporting</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText962855496904943897">This is a warm, wise, funny, heart-breaking and ultimately life-affirming book. In Macon Leary, the man who writes travel books for people who hate to travel, Tyler has created an amazing character. His damaged psyche, his vulnerability, the gradual changes in his character and outlook as he starts to connect with the messiness of living leap off the page. This book makes me laugh out loud one moment and brings tears to my eyes the next. Although Macon is the centre of the novel, the supporting characters are also wonderful creations. There's Muriel - vulnerable and needy, but alive and connected to others. There's Macon's fabulously eccentric siblings, his boss Julian, his wife Sarah and even his dog Edward - each of them real and memorable. <br /><br />Some fifteen years after last reading what is without doubt my favourite of Anne Tyler's novels, it was a joy to return to it as a buddy read with my friend Jemidar. If anything, I loved the novel even more than I did when I read and loved it all those years ago. I'm quite sure that I'll read it again.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="962855496904943897">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <a href="/user/show/1266077-stephen-gallup" class="user" title="Stephen Gallup">Stephen Gallup</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer26131437">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5829607780177574751">I’ve read and enjoyed most of Anne Tyler’s novels (starting with <em>Searching for Caleb</em>, which author Don Barthelme recommended to me years ago). A character from one of her first books (I think it was <em>If Morning Ever Comes</em>) provided the name I later gave to my daughter. <em>The Accidental Tourist</em> strikes closest to home with its theme of coping with a profound loss and then the ultimate redemption that comes from such an unexpected direction. It was while reading this book in about 1987 that I first f</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5829607780177574751">I’ve read and enjoyed most of Anne Tyler’s novels (starting with <em>Searching for Caleb</em>, which author Don Barthelme recommended to me years ago). A character from one of her first books (I think it was <em>If Morning Ever Comes</em>) provided the name I later gave to my daughter. <em>The Accidental Tourist</em> strikes closest to home with its theme of coping with a profound loss and then the ultimate redemption that comes from such an unexpected direction. It was while reading this book in about 1987 that I first felt moved to pick up a pen and begin scratching out <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10507622-what-about-the-boy-a-father-s-pledge-to-his-disabled-son">my own story</a>.<br /><br />I should say that the book and the movie are forever intertwined in my mind now: When I think of Macon and Muriel, I see William Hurt and Geena Davis. It’s very rare for the film version of any book to be anywhere near as good as the source, but in this case both are excellent. The cameo appearance of the French boy who looks just like Macon’s lost son takes my breath away every time.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="5829607780177574751">...more</a>

          </span>

      <a href="/user/show/4593541-barry-pierce" class="user" title="Barry Pierce">Barry Pierce</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/1083372.The_Accidental_Tourist" title=" 9780701129866" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/4593541-barry-pierce?shelf=20th-century" class="actionLinkLite">20th-century</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4593541-barry-pierce?shelf=read-in-2015" class="actionLinkLite">read-in-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1426871103">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11883289054024625607">Macon Leary writes travel companions under the nom de plume The Accidental Tourist. The irony is that while he helps thousands of people keep their lives together as they travel, he cannot help his own life from falling apart before his eyes.<br /><br />This is my first Anne Tyler, a writer who I've always relegated to someone that my mother might enjoy. To give context, my mother's reading habits consist of whatever was 3 for 2 in Tesco. However, since many people who I respect have given very positive rev</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11883289054024625607">Macon Leary writes travel companions under the nom de plume The Accidental Tourist. The irony is that while he helps thousands of people keep their lives together as they travel, he cannot help his own life from falling apart before his eyes.<br /><br />This is my first Anne Tyler, a writer who I've always relegated to someone that my mother might enjoy. To give context, my mother's reading habits consist of whatever was 3 for 2 in Tesco. However, since many people who I respect have given very positive reviews to Tyler in the past I thought I'd give her a go. Sadly, this didn't really do anything for me. I did enjoy the overall plot but the characters, especially Macon, were just <em>such</em> boring people. The type that you'd cross the road for if you saw them walking towards you. I found myself putting this novel down more than I picked it up. Its slice-of-life monotony is usually something that I look for in a novel but <em>The Accidental Tourist</em> just gave me... monotonous monotony. Oh well. I haven't given up all hope though. I'll definitely be visiting Anne Tyler again soon. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11883289054024625607">...more</a>

          </span>

  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/128789231" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/3446052-jemidar" class="left imgcol" title="Jemidar"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1389472953p2/3446052.jpg" alt="Jemidar" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/128789231?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 28, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3446052-jemidar" class="user" title="Jemidar">Jemidar</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/60792.The_Accidental_Tourist" title="Paperback 9780345452009" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3446052-jemidar?shelf=seen-the-movie" class="actionLinkLite">seen-the-movie</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3446052-jemidar?shelf=buddy-reads-with-kim" class="actionLinkLite">buddy-reads-with-kim</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3446052-jemidar?shelf=other-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">other-fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3446052-jemidar?shelf=favourites" class="actionLinkLite">favourites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer128789231">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16504769491459217718"><br />Buddy read with Kim.<br /><br />I first read this back in the late eighties and loved it, and recently decided to do a re-read just to see if I still loved it as much. I've changed and my life circumstances have changed, so I wondered... <br /><br />And I'm happy to say that not only do I still love it, but I think I love it a lot more than I did the first time around. Call it accumulated life experience if you like, but it had a resonance and a poignancy that touched me at a much deeper level. I laughed, I cried, I ch</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16504769491459217718"><br />Buddy read with Kim.<br /><br />I first read this back in the late eighties and loved it, and recently decided to do a re-read just to see if I still loved it as much. I've changed and my life circumstances have changed, so I wondered... <br /><br />And I'm happy to say that not only do I still love it, but I think I love it a lot more than I did the first time around. Call it accumulated life experience if you like, but it had a resonance and a poignancy that touched me at a much deeper level. I laughed, I cried, I cheered Macon on, and hissed when someone threatened to get in the way of his journey out of grief. At times his story was heartbreaking but it was ultimately uplifting, so worth every second I spent in his company. I would love to count Macon Leary amoung my friends.<br /><br />Anne Tyler is an amazing author. She makes her flawed and quirky characters so vulnerable and human, and writes about them so compassionately that you can't help but like them and empathize with them. I don't know of another author who can reach out from the page and make me feel so deeply or care so much. She is a real talent.<br /><br />I would highly recommend this book to all :-).<br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16504769491459217718">...more</a>

  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/221550300" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/360971-amy" class="left imgcol" title="Amy"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1197938725p2/360971.jpg" alt="Amy" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/221550300?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 10, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/360971-amy" class="user" title="Amy">Amy</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/60792.The_Accidental_Tourist" title="Paperback 9780345452009" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/360971-amy?shelf=didn-t-finish" class="actionLinkLite">didn-t-finish</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer221550300">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8394833180011742683">Apologies in advance to my book group. I promise to keep my mouth shut and let someone explain to me why they like this book, because I can't figure it out.<br /><br />The main character, Macon, is so compulsive and deranged. I read reviews of the book where people thought the descriptions of his daily routines were humorous. I found no humor, only desperation and pathos. His life and psychotic narrative going on in his head was too depressing for words. Reading this book made me anxious to get back to my l</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8394833180011742683">Apologies in advance to my book group. I promise to keep my mouth shut and let someone explain to me why they like this book, because I can't figure it out.<br /><br />The main character, Macon, is so compulsive and deranged. I read reviews of the book where people thought the descriptions of his daily routines were humorous. I found no humor, only desperation and pathos. His life and psychotic narrative going on in his head was too depressing for words. Reading this book made me anxious to get back to my life that I'm happy with and not try and live with such sad characters.<br /><br />Muriel was so pushy and desperate. It was not endearing, it was scary. I know there were some parts in there that were supposed to show that Macon was good for Muriel's son Alexander, but Macon and Muriel's relationship was so dysfunctional, I couldn't bear to watch Alexander tormented by their instability. I skipped ahead to try and see where their relationship was going. Muriel let that man in to her son's life knowing that he was still conflicted about his ex-wife? <br /><br />This book is not a comedy, it's not romantic, it is tragic. And the saddest part is that I imagine that there are so many people who like this story and these characters because they know people who live like this and think these are normal relationships.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="8394833180011742683">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_26528750">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/26528750" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/680205-maureen" class="left imgcol" title="Maureen"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1232569180p2/680205.jpg" alt="Maureen" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/26528750?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 07, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/680205-maureen" class="user" title="Maureen">Maureen</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/60792.The_Accidental_Tourist" title="Paperback 9780345452009" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a onclick="Effect.toggle('reviewTextContainer26528750'); return false;" href="#">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span style="display:none" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer26528750">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11009608160557297971">This books was so interesting to me. I thoroughly enjoyed the characters, especially the Leary family (they over intellectualize everything, correct grammar, and have major OCD and I felt like I could relate to them so well). Ann Tyler has a unique style of writing a novel, which left me always wanting to know more. Everything she wants to say is there...but it may be hidden in symbolism, in conversations, in small actions. It reads almost like a play, in stage directions (Macon chooses a tie) a</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11009608160557297971">This books was so interesting to me. I thoroughly enjoyed the characters, especially the Leary family (they over intellectualize everything, correct grammar, and have major OCD and I felt like I could relate to them so well). Ann Tyler has a unique style of writing a novel, which left me always wanting to know more. Everything she wants to say is there...but it may be hidden in symbolism, in conversations, in small actions. It reads almost like a play, in stage directions (Macon chooses a tie) and conversation. You have to read a little between the lines to catch the wealth of story that Tyler is offering.<br /><br />I found myself very pleased with the end of the novel, which surprised me. I like Ann Tyler's way of sneaking up on you through an interesting story and then revealing to you at the end that what you believed were absolutes are actually gray areas (Barbara Kingsolver does this to me too). <br /><br />From my standpoint, the (morally) right thing, the thing Macon should have done, was to try to stay with his wife. But, they weren't a good match, they no longer had children together, Muriel was so much better for him...and so I felt like he made the right choice, despite all I personally believe(d?) to the contrary. Which left me feeling...uncomfortable. Because more black and whites have just been proven grays after all...<br /><br />But I realized that the book is not about deciding to leave a marriage or make it work. Macon and Sarah's marriage is really meant to illustrate people (like Macon) who lead "accidental" lives, who never "take steps." Tyler shows us that people who are trapped in their grooves, like the entire Leary clan, can "take steps" and can change and let new things and new experiences into their lives. Macon is a man who has always done things the same way, because it has been a way that has worked for him. After his son's death, however, it no longer became an adequate method for coping with life. To me this story is so hopeful and happy because Macon does find a new way of life and he realizes that there is not one right way to live, there can be many, and that is what makes life so full.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11009608160557297971">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

I still am in awe of how such a slow story without any real standout events could make me miss it while I was at work and hate to turn to page and be one more closer to the end. I didn't particulary care for any of the characters until the end(except for the brash and tacky Muriel whom I loved all along). You will love Macon's transformation and watching him learn to live, not again, but for the first time ever.               <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1643578">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5676250426126711181">I guess this will always be one of my all time favourite books. For me, it worked on all levels, I loved the story, characters and the routine absurdities that form part and parecel of everyday life. There is tragedy, humour and romance. I think this is the best book Anne Tylor has written and I've read all of them. Nowhere else does she captures the nuances of relationships so well. On a personal level, this book will always mean a lot to me, introducing a kind of anal retentive anti hero who y</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5676250426126711181">I guess this will always be one of my all time favourite books. For me, it worked on all levels, I loved the story, characters and the routine absurdities that form part and parecel of everyday life. There is tragedy, humour and romance. I think this is the best book Anne Tylor has written and I've read all of them. Nowhere else does she captures the nuances of relationships so well. On a personal level, this book will always mean a lot to me, introducing a kind of anal retentive anti hero who yet manages to be both appealing and desirable. We learn that organisation is a fear of chaos and that sometimes the organised amongst us must venture into the chaotic to fully realise our potential. It also taught me that heroism comes in many shapes and forms and that it is not always the handsome and strong who caspture our hearts.</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer91482850">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8264520949988872930">I am an unabashed Ann Tyler fanboy. She can write about things that in another author`s hands would be mundane or cliched but with her remain completely riveting, warm and funny and desperately sad. The Accidental Tourist is the story of a man with very limited ability to handle change who in the aftermath of his sons death tries to live. This may not sound like the funniest scenario ever but there are some great moments. Loved it.</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8264520949988872930">I am an unabashed Ann Tyler fanboy. She can write about things that in another author`s hands would be mundane or cliched but with her remain completely riveting, warm and funny and desperately sad. The Accidental Tourist is the story of a man with very limited ability to handle change who in the aftermath of his sons death tries to live. This may not sound like the funniest scenario ever but there are some great moments. Loved it.</span>

The wife comes back. I don't know who I want him to be with, since his life has somewhat changed for the better with the younger woman, and she saves him from his bitter, OCD life, but he does still love his wife and to me marriage is a sacred bond... so who should h</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6771244288535305077">Things I liked about the book: humorous details, the symbolism (the house, the dog), driving plot<br /><br />Things I am not sure that I like: the guy's wife leaves him and he "takes up" with a vibrant young woman who has a kid and a hard life. The wife comes back. I don't know who I want him to be with, since his life has somewhat changed for the better with the younger woman, and she saves him from his bitter, OCD life, but he does still love his wife and to me marriage is a sacred bond... so who should he be with? I don't know that there is a clean answer to that question, and the ending is as messy as life. The final paragraph was beautiful; it satisfied my sense of aesthetics even if it didn't satisfy me on other levels</span>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4639959638037687318">I first read this book about 25 years ago,I gave it three &amp; half stars at that time,the book is the same but I am not. It gets five stars today. I understand the Macon<br />Leary so much better now. He seams to be so lonely in a crowd. A year after the death of has son he is still in mourning &amp; is unable to open up even to his wife.<br />In the opening chapter his wife leaves him because of this, shortly after this he &amp; Edward ( his sons dog) move back to the home he grew up in with his sister &amp; two<br />brothers. Sometime later he has to leave go on a trip and has to board edward at an animal hospital ( his brothers &amp; sister are afraid of him) this is where he meets Muriel &amp; his life changes . Slowly with Muriel he begins to open up &amp; enjoy life again.<br />On the cover of the paperback book from 25 years ago their is a small snipit from the Washington Post,I didn't notice it the first time around &amp; it sayes the following<br />----one cannot reasonably expect fiction to be much better than this-----I am going to spend the rest of this year(or however long it takes) rereading all the books<br />That I had given five stars to,just to see if they meet that standard.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_304527461">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/304527461" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/8040729-nereia" class="left imgcol" title="Nereia"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1426402618p2/8040729.jpg" alt="Nereia" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/304527461?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 11, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/8040729-nereia" class="user" title="Nereia">Nereia</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/12493681-turista-per-caso" title="Paperback 9788850224319" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer304527461">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6295817726216861880"><em>Una boccata d'aria fresca</em><br /><br />Mi piace leggere Anne Tyler, perché mi rilassa, mi diverte, mi rende serena. Ogniqualvolta mi sento con l'acqua alla gola, ogniqualvolta vivo un periodo cupo e contrassegnato dal più tremendo dei malumori prendo in mano un libro scritto da Anne Tyler. Le sue storie, seppur mai troppo originali o sorprendenti, riescono a trasportami in un mondo parallelo, dove la vita viene vissuta con più leggerezza.<br />Le parole di Turista per caso scorrono velocemente e ogni capoverso cost</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6295817726216861880"><em>Una boccata d'aria fresca</em><br /><br />Mi piace leggere Anne Tyler, perché mi rilassa, mi diverte, mi rende serena. Ogniqualvolta mi sento con l'acqua alla gola, ogniqualvolta vivo un periodo cupo e contrassegnato dal più tremendo dei malumori prendo in mano un libro scritto da Anne Tyler. Le sue storie, seppur mai troppo originali o sorprendenti, riescono a trasportami in un mondo parallelo, dove la vita viene vissuta con più leggerezza.<br />Le parole di Turista per caso scorrono velocemente e ogni capoverso costituisce un passo verso una finestra aperta. Perché, se prima di iniziarne la lettura mi trovavo costretta in una piccola stanza buia e afosa, ogni capitolo mi permetteva di avvicinarmi sempre di più ad un'agognata boccata d'aria fresca. Questo libro è proprio da leggere così, "a pieni polmoni".<br />La storia narrata, in verità, non può essere definita il punto forte del romanzo. Macon, come tutti i componenti della famiglia Leary, è ad un passo dall'essere affetto dal disturbo ossessivo compulsivo.<br />Possiede un sistema, un metodo, per qualunque cosa, anche per ciò che apparentemente può sembrare insignificante. I sistemi lo rendono tranquillo, costituiscono le basi della sua quotidianità.<br />Una tragedia, rappresentata dalla brutale morte del suo unico figlio, minaccia di rovinare il suo equilibrio messo in pericolo, tra le altre cose, dalla decisione di sua moglie Sarah di troncare il loro matrimonio.<br />Inizia proprio così il libro della Tyler, a tragedia già avvenuta, mostrandoci Macon e Sarah come due persone stanche della loro situazione coniuguale. Ma è Sarah e non Macon, tra i due, ad aver perso la voglia di lottare per un matrimonio nel quale ormai non ha più la forza di credere.<br />Macon, inizialmente, non la prende bene e cerca di reagire al dolore come solo un componente della famiglia Leary sa fare: creando inutili e assurdi sistemi. Un sistema per evitare di fare le scale, un sistema per sistemare la spesa nella dispensa, un sistema per lavare il bucato.<br />Tra le cose che più ho apprezzato in questo romanzo vi sono, appunto, le particolareggiate descrizioni di tutti i sistemi che Macon crea, credendo fermamente che gli facilitino la vita e la rendano più confortevole, meno esrtanea ed estraniante. L'autrice li descrive così dettagliatamente quasi a voler convincere il lettore che, tutto sommato, una loro logica la possiedano pure.<br />Interessanti e perché no, a loro modo anche divertenti, i discutibili metodi escogitati da Rose, la sorella di Macon, per portare avanti la casa e prendersi cura di tutti coloro che la circondano, come solo una vera chioccia sa fare.<br />Anne Tyler, attraverso una scrittura fluida e leggera, e tramite qualche flashback sapientemente posizionato qua e là, riesce a fornire un profilo psicologico molto dettagliato di ogni personaggio, senza tralasciare i personaggi secondari.<br />Che si trattasse di un'autrice brava e dannatamente competente, d'altronde, me ne ero già accorta leggendo Una donna diversa (il cui titolo italiano non assomiglia nemmeno vagamente a quello originale, senza dubbio più azzeccato: Looking for Jacob), libro letto diverso tempo fa ma del quale conservo un grazioso ricordo.<br />L'unica pecca di questo romanzo, altrimenti davvero molto bello, è la traduzione che ne è stata fatta dall'inglese all'italiano. Tantissimi, troppi ed eclatanti errori, uniti alle parecchie imprecisioni e ai termini in disuso ne rendono fastidiosa la lettura. Si tratta di un'opera del 1985, tradotta solamente un anno dopo dalla sua pubblicazione negli Stati Uniti d'America e quindi è forse imputabile a questo l'utilizzo di termini arcaici, vintage, demodè. Probabilmente, però, nemmeno nel 1985 si usava più la parola italiana "paltò" come traduzione di un semplicissimo "coat"(cappotto).<br /><br />Recensione presente anche sul mio blog: <a rel="nofollow" href="http://librangoloacuto.blogspot.it/2012/04/recensione-turista-per-caso.html">Recensione di Turista per caso</a></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6295817726216861880">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/170601599" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1036893-fabian" class="left imgcol" title="Fabian"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1449595249p2/1036893.jpg" alt="Fabian" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/170601599?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 27, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1036893-fabian" class="user" title="Fabian">Fabian</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/60792.The_Accidental_Tourist" title="Paperback 9780345452009" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer170601599">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13417882723663029299">Accidental tourists are annoying! (These are those pesky travelers who refuse to give up all their customs, their comforts; refuse to get lost a little in the foreigness, to LIVE.) <br /><br />And this book isn't. A success then!--considering the subject matter. Yeah, the protagonist is a huge bore and as he has one of the best jobs of all time is doubly douche-ey, but he has a reason to be maudlin and dissatisfied. Lifetime Movie Network viewers would have a blast... and the novel feels dated indeed. But T</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13417882723663029299">Accidental tourists are annoying! (These are those pesky travelers who refuse to give up all their customs, their comforts; refuse to get lost a little in the foreigness, to LIVE.) <br /><br />And this book isn't. A success then!--considering the subject matter. Yeah, the protagonist is a huge bore and as he has one of the best jobs of all time is doubly douche-ey, but he has a reason to be maudlin and dissatisfied. Lifetime Movie Network viewers would have a blast... and the novel feels dated indeed. But Tyler does a great job in making all characters believable and all situations credible... you feel very bad for the guy you basically would hate to have around you. His intellectual edge is miniscle, and you feel bad for all other "dumber" characters too. It's slightly symbolic, but also rather... small.<br /><br />It is wise to note that other books by this particular publishing company such as "The Patron Saint of Liars" by Anne Patchett and "The World According to Garp" by John Irvin also seem to fit within this category of above-average reads--which you may or may not be inspired to recommend, depending on the mood, the weather, the person.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13417882723663029299">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

It was pitch dark, but through an open window he heard distant laughter, a strain of music, faint cheers as if some sort of game were going on. He squinted at the clock radio: three thirty. And on this street-this worn, sad street where nothing went right for anyone, where the men had dead-end jobs or none at all and the women were running to fat and the children were</em></span>

But another cheer went up, and someone sang a line from a song. Macon found himself smiling. He turned toward Muriel and closed his eyes; he slept dreamlessly the rest of the night. </em></span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer293546968">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15576972512945707708">A decent read, but I didn't love it, for the following reasons:<br /><br />1. The dog training scenes were unrealistic, and borderline cruel. I realize this isn't a dog training book. I only hope that Anne Tyler is a cat person.<br /><br />2. Muriel's desperation was overwhelming, and off-putting.<br /><br />3. My usual complaint about character development and show-versus-tell. I did not discover Macon, he was handed to me as a pre-packaged collection of quirks and tragic back story.<br /><br /></span>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer12196437">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14955245082230630368">If you're interested in reading a book that will challenge every single emotion you thought was possible.....this one will not disappoint. I was able to step inside the psyche of every single character and understand to the fullest extent their feelings of loss, fear, sadness,desperation and frustration.....simply because I have been there myself.<br />This story will reveal what really happens when someone loses a child. <br />Best have your Kleenex closeby.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a onclick="Effect.toggle('reviewTextContainer1290529880'); return false;" href="#">click here.</a>

              <span style="display:none" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1290529880">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15191913815485217482">Anne Tyler is fast becoming a favorite author. Her writing style is realistic and down-to-earth, and her characters flawed, eccentric, and oddly lovable. <br /><br />I liked this book, but didn't love it and I think it's because the ending was a little baffling. Macon, the protagonist, had to choose between two love interests: Sarah, his wife of 21 years who he'd grown distant from in the wake of their son's murder, and a much younger, flamboyant dog trainer named Muriel who helped him to loosen up and shar</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15191913815485217482">Anne Tyler is fast becoming a favorite author. Her writing style is realistic and down-to-earth, and her characters flawed, eccentric, and oddly lovable. <br /><br />I liked this book, but didn't love it and I think it's because the ending was a little baffling. Macon, the protagonist, had to choose between two love interests: Sarah, his wife of 21 years who he'd grown distant from in the wake of their son's murder, and a much younger, flamboyant dog trainer named Muriel who helped him to loosen up and share his feelings. In the end he picks the latter but I think it might've just been because he liked who he was with Muriel more even though he loved his wife more. I'm still not sure how I feel about that. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="15191913815485217482">...more</a>

          </span>

          <a href="/book/show/22465465-the-accidental-tourist" title="Audible Audio " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/4999879-linda?shelf=contemporary-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">contemporary-fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4999879-linda?shelf=audio" class="actionLinkLite">audio</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4999879-linda?shelf=literary" class="actionLinkLite">literary</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4999879-linda?shelf=real-life" class="actionLinkLite">real-life</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1349089020">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12686034949513419875">This is pre-9/11 when air travel was a lot simpler - you won't find a cockpit without a door these days, but they did exist on some of those really small regional planes. So keep in mind that the setting is 1985 not 2015 and you'll enjoy this even more.<br /><br />Macon and Sara have lost their 12 year old son -- while at summer camp he was murdered in a burger joint by robber (today, it would be an angry man with a automatic rifle). As often happens to couples after such a tragedy, they are not doing well.</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12686034949513419875">This is pre-9/11 when air travel was a lot simpler - you won't find a cockpit without a door these days, but they did exist on some of those really small regional planes. So keep in mind that the setting is 1985 not 2015 and you'll enjoy this even more.<br /><br />Macon and Sara have lost their 12 year old son -- while at summer camp he was murdered in a burger joint by robber (today, it would be an angry man with a automatic rifle). As often happens to couples after such a tragedy, they are not doing well. Sara leaves. Macon barely survives - his OCD takes over. Soon he finds himself back in the old family home with his sister (never married) and two brothers (both divorced). They are four of a kind - all have OCD. <br /><br />Macon is the narrator and we live with him in his pain and his slow reawakening. But we also learn much about his siblings, his boss/best friend, Sara, and Macon's girlfriend Muriel. This is real life. It is messy. There is not clean ending but why should there be. Life is rarely anything but messy, despite attempts to structure it to keep the messiness at bay. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12686034949513419875">...more</a>

          </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1216935-nolan?shelf=nls-audio" class="actionLinkLite">nls-audio</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1360436202">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2931507015572446687">Macon Leary and his wife have tried to make their marriage succeed after their child dies. But his strange organize-everything OCD that she once tolerated is now more than she can handle. The marriage began falling apart after their young son was killed in a holdup, and his bizarre behavior combines with her grief to be more than the 20-year union can handle.<br /><br />He moves in with his sister and brothers; she gets her own place; he meets a flighty flaky woman who initially seems more eager to point ou</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2931507015572446687">Macon Leary and his wife have tried to make their marriage succeed after their child dies. But his strange organize-everything OCD that she once tolerated is now more than she can handle. The marriage began falling apart after their young son was killed in a holdup, and his bizarre behavior combines with her grief to be more than the 20-year union can handle.<br /><br />He moves in with his sister and brothers; she gets her own place; he meets a flighty flaky woman who initially seems more eager to point out her divorced status than to tell him that she trains dogs. Macon is a travel writer who hates to travel, and at least the dog trainer manages to put some zip in his otherwise zipless life.<br /><br />Others have pronounced this book poignant and funny; it left me feeling hopeless or something close to it. I won't spoil the end, but I wish fervently that it had turned out differently. I never developed a sense of closeness to an? of these characters. Tyler is a tremendous success at the craft of writing; I certainly don't want to in any way marginalize her talent. I intend to read other books by her; this one just didn't do much for me in terms of helping me connect to it.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/466454095?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 07, 2016</a>

      <a href="/user/show/6915394-kristy-miller" class="user" title="Kristy Miller">Kristy Miller</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/60792.The_Accidental_Tourist" title="Paperback 9780345452009" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer466454095">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1659637886017663232">This is the second Anne Tyler book for me. Interestingly, the first one was also about a grieving middle-aged man; I wonder if that’s a recurring theme for her. I picked this one up as an audible deal of the day a while back, knowing that it was her first big book and one of her most popular ones. <br />At first I thought that it was a perfectly decent book, even if it wasn’t one that I particularly liked. Macon Leary is a travel writer who hates travel and hates change. After the violent death of his</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1659637886017663232">This is the second Anne Tyler book for me. Interestingly, the first one was also about a grieving middle-aged man; I wonder if that’s a recurring theme for her. I picked this one up as an audible deal of the day a while back, knowing that it was her first big book and one of her most popular ones. <br />At first I thought that it was a perfectly decent book, even if it wasn’t one that I particularly liked. Macon Leary is a travel writer who hates travel and hates change. After the violent death of his son, he and his wife Sarah are separated, and Macon is struggling after breaking his leg. He gets drawn in to a relationship with Muriel, a woman who is helping him train his erratic corgi, Edward. Macon is consistently described as stuffy, and is a slightly boring character. Muriel is a 25 year old woman, divorced with a 7 year old son, and is all over the place. She’s eccentric, flighty, and barely holds her life together working multiple odd jobs. <br />I never bought the idea of Macon and Muriel as a couple. While I know odd couples exist Ms. Tyler never made them seem like a real, viable possibility. Macon is feckless and Muriel is manipulative and infuriating. Neither of the characters is capable of having a straight forward, honest conversation. <br />I did not like this book, and I do not recommend it.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1659637886017663232">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_173596214">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/173596214" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2852338-adam-wilson" class="left imgcol" title="Adam Wilson"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" alt="Adam Wilson" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/173596214?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 04, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2852338-adam-wilson" class="user" title="Adam Wilson">Adam Wilson</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/60792.The_Accidental_Tourist" title="Paperback 9780345452009" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer173596214">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8942142822986612661">The Accidental Tourist really surprised me. I have never read Anne Tyler before and I don’t usually get into general fiction like this but this was, to put it very simply, a beautiful novel and story. It is amazingly well-written, the characters are totally unique but believable, and the plot is interesting from beginning to end. I lost just a little bit of interest near the end when the book seemed to turn into a romance, but most stories involve love and the choices that go with love so this w</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8942142822986612661">The Accidental Tourist really surprised me. I have never read Anne Tyler before and I don’t usually get into general fiction like this but this was, to put it very simply, a beautiful novel and story. It is amazingly well-written, the characters are totally unique but believable, and the plot is interesting from beginning to end. I lost just a little bit of interest near the end when the book seemed to turn into a romance, but most stories involve love and the choices that go with love so this wasn’t much of an issue with me. Also, I am one of those people who loves a book involving a disobedient dog. Edward, from this novel, fits that description nicely and Macon’s efforts to tame him are hilarious. Most importantly for me, and I know it is something I always mention, was the brilliance in the characterization. Anne Tyler really seems to understand people. Not just a few types of people but people in general. Whenever her characters surprised me in this book, I would be shocked but I would always accept their actions as reasonable even if they weren’t predictable.<br />In short, a book that I am proud to have read. With the millions of books in the world that we will never have time to get to, it is nice to read one that I know I loved and will remember, instead of wishing I hadn’t wasted my limited reading time on it. I recommend this to absolutely everyone. <br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="8942142822986612661">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/521405635?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 30, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3574288-janice-williams" class="user" title="Janice Williams">Janice Williams</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/60792.The_Accidental_Tourist" title="Paperback 9780345452009" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3574288-janice-williams?shelf=fiction" class="actionLinkLite">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer521405635">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7320375215189357111">I read this book a few years ago and just reread it for the second time. (The copyright is 1985). It's a wonderful book, because, of course, Tyler's writing is so seamless, every word easing the story along, but also because of the characters in this book. For "The Accidental Tourist" is about love and about living one's life, and about families; but what stands out to me are the characters and how Tyler brings them to life. <br /><br />You never really know how the main character, Macon, will make it throu</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7320375215189357111">I read this book a few years ago and just reread it for the second time. (The copyright is 1985). It's a wonderful book, because, of course, Tyler's writing is so seamless, every word easing the story along, but also because of the characters in this book. For "The Accidental Tourist" is about love and about living one's life, and about families; but what stands out to me are the characters and how Tyler brings them to life. <br /><br />You never really know how the main character, Macon, will make it through the months following a marital separation on the heels of his son's murder, but watching him interact with the quirky, outspoken character of Muriel, as well as his publisher-boss, Julian, and siblings, Rose, Charles, and Porter, is a captivating journey. Will he and his wife, Sarah, reconcile? Will he choose Muriel? Will his dog ever behave? These are questions that kept me reading. <br /><br />Also, setting this story within the concept of The Accidental Tourist, a set of travel guides for businessmen who want to feel as if they are still at home, is, from a writer's craft point-of-view, a wonderful tool that totally works and adds a layer to this book that, well, could not be separated from the story. It is perfect.<br /><br />Since Anne Tyler is such a well-regarded, well-known writer, I'm sure there are many reviews out there for this book. But I wanted to say why I like it so much and recommend it to my friends. I'm sure I will read it for a third time in a few years. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7320375215189357111">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_50541626">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/50541626" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1294343-kara" class="left imgcol" title="Kara"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" alt="Kara" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/50541626?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 01, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1294343-kara" class="user" title="Kara">Kara</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/60792.The_Accidental_Tourist" title="Paperback 9780345452009" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer50541626">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8548371084692744635">I didn't know this was an old book until I began reading it and noticed some references that dated the book. I also didn't know it had been made into a movie! Neither of these facts influenced my mixed opinion of the book.<br /><br />I enjoyed the author's writing style and ability to illustrate the way seemingly tedious events influence the path of one's life as much as big events do. The author also did a wonderful job of demonstrating how difficult it is to break away from one's comfort zone and what the</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8548371084692744635">I didn't know this was an old book until I began reading it and noticed some references that dated the book. I also didn't know it had been made into a movie! Neither of these facts influenced my mixed opinion of the book.<br /><br />I enjoyed the author's writing style and ability to illustrate the way seemingly tedious events influence the path of one's life as much as big events do. The author also did a wonderful job of demonstrating how difficult it is to break away from one's comfort zone and what the rewards can be once you do. I thought the characters, except one, were more akin to the tedious events than the big, interesting ones and often found myself struggling to get through the book. <br /><br />The character who initially attracted me to the book was a dog trainer. My high hopes for her were dashed as soon as the author noted her use of a choke collar, but still, I gave her a chance. In the end I was turned off by her over the top "uniqueness." I should note that her training techniques were typical for the mid-80's, but it did influence my opinion of her.<br /><br />Overall, I thought it was "okay" and helped to pass the time. It is not a book I would recommend, nor will I keep it on my bookshelf. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="8548371084692744635">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer445314579">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8823123337154666995">Our latest book club novel, and I gave it the highest score out of 5 of all our members. Most people thought it was ok, a few didn't like it, particularly the ending.<br />This is the story of a group of pretty dysfunctional characters, focussing on the main guy, Macon. His marriage goes awry, following the tragic murder of his young son, and this book is really about him rediscovering his life and eventually changing direction. The book is littered with ancillary characters, including Macon's 3 sibli</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8823123337154666995">Our latest book club novel, and I gave it the highest score out of 5 of all our members. Most people thought it was ok, a few didn't like it, particularly the ending.<br />This is the story of a group of pretty dysfunctional characters, focussing on the main guy, Macon. His marriage goes awry, following the tragic murder of his young son, and this book is really about him rediscovering his life and eventually changing direction. The book is littered with ancillary characters, including Macon's 3 siblings, all who share the same weird foibles. <br />I'm quite keen to see if I can find a copy of the 1988 film made of The Accidental Tourist, starring William Hurt, Kathleen Turner and Geena Davis. I think it could translate well to celluloid. </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('rHWZ+5B6W82kvBR/NOalDCKxwDC6KFjFZnJW+pL5PvzJoaYoYqhPNyhkYMRKh0O+a0YDKfP1H28Me1NoXmzIuQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&amp;book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;refresh=true' + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('SWmw+1pbk31OWIvfoPdwk9DOsgK5+0T8VP+/PcS9qeQsvY8oqImHh8KA/2TelpYhmTlxG/AmA1Y+9rqvCChfoQ==')})
  }
//]]&gt;
</script>

Much to her surprise, she finds herself drawn to the life she encounters in Iran; intoxicated by each exotic sight which reminds her how far from home she really is; both comforted and unsettled by the group of foreign and Iranian physicians and their wives who take her in.     <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/457.Anne_Tyler">About Anne Tyler</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/457.Anne_Tyler"><img alt="457" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1332881249p2/457.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer17479426086097279377"><strong>Anne Tyler</strong> was born in Minneapolis, Minnesota, in 1941 and grew up in Raleigh, North Carolina. She graduated at nineteen from Duke University and went on to do graduate work in Russian studies at Columbia University. <em> <a title="The Beginner's Goodbye by Anne Tyler" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12482658.The_Beginner_s_Goodbye">The Beginner's Goodbye</a> </em> is Anne Tyler's nineteenth novel; her eleventh, <em> <a title="Breathing Lessons by Anne Tyler" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/31181.Breathing_Lessons">Breathing Lessons</a> </em>, was awarded the Pulitzer Prize in 1988. She is a member of the American Academy of Arts a</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17479426086097279377"><strong>Anne Tyler</strong> was born in Minneapolis, Minnesota, in 1941 and grew up in Raleigh, North Carolina. She graduated at nineteen from Duke University and went on to do graduate work in Russian studies at Columbia University. <em>
  <a title="The Beginner's Goodbye by Anne Tyler" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12482658.The_Beginner_s_Goodbye">The Beginner's Goodbye</a>
</em> is Anne Tyler's nineteenth novel; her eleventh, <em>
  <a title="Breathing Lessons by Anne Tyler" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/31181.Breathing_Lessons">Breathing Lessons</a>
</em>, was awarded the Pulitzer Prize in 1988. She is a member of the American Academy of Arts and Letters.</span>
